Feeling Threatened by Japan and Germany, the Soviet Union Consolidates National Defense; Red Army Strength 1.3 Million; Eastern and Western Borders Sufficient to Resist Strong Enemies 43

Moscow

At today's meeting of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union, Deputy Minister of Defense General Tukhachevsky announced that the Red Army now has a total of 1.3 million people, of which 77% have been trained and possess weapons. Everyone cheered loudly upon hearing his words. Tukhachevsky also said that the monthly salary of soldiers will be increased by 50% this year. Tukhachevsky continued to mention that the increase in military equipment by Germany and Japan is harming the Soviet Union and forcing it to greatly increase the national defense expenditure in this year's budget proposal. The military expenditure in 1936 is twice that of last year. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Moscow

Soviet Deputy Minister of Defense Tukhachevsky spoke during the discussion of the government budget and received a long ovation from the conference. He said, "Military expenditure is indeed not a small number, but the proportion it occupies in the entire budget is still smaller than that of various countries. It goes without saying that it is especially true for countries that are eagerly preparing for a war of aggression. What still needs to be said is that this number is still very small from the perspective of the practical tasks of national defense organizations. Tukhachevsky pointed out the threat to the Soviet Union in the Far East from Japan, and the threat to the west from Germany, detailing the war-mongering fervor of the two countries. He continued, "The situation on our eastern and western borders makes us demand serious consideration of our national defense equipment. The east and west borders are 10,000 kilometers apart and must have simultaneous and independent national defense. This is a necessary principle. In addition, the military force on our western border has greatly increased compared to previous years, so we must strengthen our standing army. Until now, our local troops accounted for 74%, and our standing army accounted for 26%. In order to strengthen the standing army to resist unexpected attacks, we accepted Stalin's suggestion (applause) and reorganized the Red Army infantry according to the opposite principle, that is, the standing army accounted for 77%, and the local troops accounted for 23%. At the same time, the establishment of the standing army can be transferred to war in a timely manner. The extensive increase in the combat effectiveness of our infantry not only creates constant combat readiness but also completes the most complete military training. The cost of expanding the army according to this principle is naturally huge, but this principle guarantees the rapid completion of military training from peacetime to wartime, and it is the most perfect from the perspective of mobilization and military training. When the government needs it, we can immediately resist any strong enemy on both our east and west borders with a strong and prepared force." She continued to describe the development of mechanized and cavalry teams, making them easier to deploy and suitable for national defense, and enhancing the strength of air defense, and emphasized the development of various aviation, and allowed to pay attention to independent aviation, which is the most powerful tool of modern warfare. "Those who dream of seizing Soviet territory have to consider the Soviet Union's aviation power, and they must also consider that they will encounter unexpected difficulties if they want to use air force to attack most of the Soviet Union's industrial centers (and our enemies do not have this benefit).

Tukhachevsky mentioned the development of safety parachute jumping, saying that tens of thousands of Red Army soldiers have obtained safety parachute badges. In addition, the Soviet Civil Aviation Club has made 16,000 airplane jumps and more than 800,000 safety parachute tower jumps.

Tukhachevsky mentioned the navy, saying, "We are now building a strong navy, first focusing on the development of submarines, but in the future, in addition to building submarines, we will also rapidly develop surface forces. Our navy will gradually become stronger and stronger, to the same level as the army and air force." He continued to describe the consolidation of coastal defense and the increase in seaplane power by several times, and filling it with the latest aircraft, and said, "Our development of the navy is to thicken the coastal defense on both the east and west sides. This goes without saying. These various methods of strengthening national defense will necessarily strengthen the overall military force." In 1936, the strength of the Red Army will increase to 1.3 million people (cheers, applause, followed by cheers to Stalin and Voroshilov).

Tukhachevsky reported on the completion of the slogan put forward by Stalin, "Create cadres and make them control technology," pointing out that the adoption of military titles created a solid foundation for cultivating commanders and technical cadres. The number of aviation, armored vehicle, artillery, and infantry schools has greatly increased. The equipment of these schools has been greatly improved to improve the training of experts. The Red Army has 13 military academies to cultivate various specialized talents, and there are six military specialized schools affiliated to ordinary universities. There are more than 16,000 students in military academies. The flying fields and shooting ranges for training troops have also greatly increased. The cultural and living conditions of the Red Army have greatly improved, and the soldiers' pay has also increased. The amount of pay in 1936 increased by 57%. Tukhachevsky reiterated the annual improvement of the Red Army's work and organization, and the elimination of various shortcomings, saying that "because of this, our work has guaranteed that the military training of the Red Army will reach an extremely high level that no other country can match." Finally, he said, "I hope that the conference will approve the military budget. If so, the Red Army and all its personnel will be able to devote all their strength and enthusiasm to controlling the complex art of modern warfare, and under the leadership of our leaders Voroshilov in the party and Stalin, if the enemy attacks the border, they will respond with a complete victory." Tukhachevsky's concluding remarks were submerged in applause. The conference cheered long live Stalin, Voroshilov, and the Red Army. (15th TASS Dispatch)

The Soviet Union's New Budget: Totaling 78.5 Billion Rubles; Military Expenditure Nearly Doubled Compared to Last Year 44

Moscow

People's Commissar of Finance Klinko spoke on the 1936 national budget at the Second Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union, saying, "In 1935, the income budget was 63.6 billion rubles, and the actual income was 64.6 billion rubles. The expenditure budget was 63.1 billion rubles, and the actual expenditure was 63.9 billion rubles. Therefore, last year's income exceeded expenditure by 700 million rubles, which is a huge contribution to socialist construction. The main items in last year's budget were all completed, and some items were even exceeded. Due to the success of socialist construction and the complete abolition of the bread coupon system, commodity trade increased from 60 billion rubles to 80 billion rubles. In the Soviet Union, the Soviet ruble is only a medium of exchange, so it is more stable than any currency in the world."

Klinko continued to describe the 1936 budget, saying that the government budget for 1936 fully reflects the strong development of socialist construction in 1936. The total amount of this resolution budget reached 78.5 billion rubles, which is more than 14 billion rubles higher than last year's settlement. Due to the Stakhanovite movement, the efforts of various enterprises to increase profits, and the increase in the total profits of various economic organizations, the new budget also increased by a percentage of. Klinko continued to describe the expenditure, saying that the amount of construction investment reached 32.3 billion rubles, and the budget for national defense expenditure was even more approved by the conference with special applause. Klinko pointed out that national defense expenditure was larger in 1935, with a budget of 6.5 billion rubles and an actual expenditure of 8.2 billion rubles. The national defense expenditure in 1936 will increase to 14.8 billion rubles. Klinko said, "The increase in national defense expenditure is to increase military strength and improve its technical equipment, expand barracks, and increase political education expenditure." Klinko continued to describe the amount of expenditure on social and cultural undertakings, which also increased from 16 billion rubles to 21 billion rubles this year, excluding those spent by trade unions, a total increase of 5 billion rubles. The construction of schools has greatly increased, and the number of schoolchildren has increased to 28 million this year. The expenditure for training cadres and talents has almost increased by 1 billion rubles. The expenditure on public health has increased from 4.7 billion to 6.2 billion rubles. Klinko said, "The 1936 budget is obviously based on the general increase in national wealth, and the continued development of socialist construction can not only be completed but also exceeded."

The amount of investment in housing construction and urban construction is 5.57 billion rubles, and the retail sales of state-owned cooperative stores are 100 billion rubles, and retail prices will be reduced in 1936. The total number of workers and employees will reach 25,725,000, and the wage fund will increase from 56.2 billion rubles in 1935 to 63.4 billion rubles in 1936. Social and cultural expenses will increase by 33.6% compared to 1935, reaching 17.638 billion rubles. The social insurance expenditure is 8 billion rubles, while it was 6.7 billion rubles in 1935.

In 1936, there will be 85,300 students graduating from universities and technical specialized schools, and 138,100 people graduating from ordinary technical schools. The fourth year of the Second Five-Year Plan guarantees the considerable consolidation of the country's political and economic strength, and further promotes its technical and economic independence and its national defense strength. The implementation of this plan is to complete the four years of the Second Five-Year Plan in all major parts of the national economy, and to guarantee the early completion of the entire Five-Year Plan. The Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union proves the firm expectation of the Soviet people for peace and supports the resolute implementation of the peace policy of the People's Committee. At the same time, the Central Executive Committee believes that the unconditional completion of the economic tasks in 1936 and the consolidation of the Soviet Union's national defense strength on this basis are necessary conditions for completing the policy of striving for peace. (15th TASS Dispatch)

Mongolian-Manchurian Border Disputes: Manchuria Threatens to Take Decisive Action; Exchange of Documents Published; Russian Dispatch Reports Japanese-Manchurian Troops Invading Mongolian Border Again 45

Moscow

The Mongolian government and the "Manchukuo" government recently exchanged sternly worded documents regarding border cases. A document from the "Manchukuo" Foreign Ministry to the Mongolian government on December 25 stated that it would disregard everything and take practical countermeasures. Three days later, it issued another document stating that it would be forced to implement any necessary plans for self-defense. The Mongolian government replied on January 12, saying that the nature and wording of the letter were sufficient to prove that the "Manchukuo" government did not want to peacefully resolve the border cases caused by the Japanese and "Manchukuo" soldiers, and to prevent the continuation of similar incidents that clearly intended to cause disputes between the two sides. The Mongolian people are now devoting all their efforts to economic and cultural development. No one in the world believes that they will plot to engage in war with Japan or provoke Japanese and "Manchukuo" troops. The Mongolian government asked "Manchukuo" to pay attention to the serious danger to peace contained in the continued invasion of the Mongolian border, and that the Mongolian soldiers detained by the "Manchukuo" side should be released immediately. According to the report, both sides are now vying for the land where the incident was initiated, which is within their own borders. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Kulun The Kulun report said that the local newspapers have published the exchange of documents between the Mongolian People's Republic and "Manchukuo" regarding the attack on the Mongolian border by Japanese-Manchurian troops on December 9, 1935. The "Manchukuo" Foreign Minister issued a document on December 25, replying to the protest raised by the Mongolian government on December 22. The document falsely claimed that the conflict between the Japanese-Manchurian troops and the Mongolian border guards occurred within "Manchukuo" territory, the reason being that the Mongolian troops invaded the Manchukuo border, and stated that "regardless of the outcome, decisive action will be taken."

On December 24, Japanese-Manchurian troops attempted to attack the Mongolian border guard camp in the Brantson area again, but were unsuccessful due to the resistance of the Mongolian border guards. The "Manchukuo" Foreign Minister therefore issued another note to the Mongolian government on December 28, falsely claiming that the attack on the Mongolian border by Japanese-Manchurian troops was a Mongolian troop attack on the "peaceful" Manchukuo troops, and attached a protest, and again made the threat of "in the future, any necessary self-defense actions may be forced to be adopted."

The government of the Mongolian Republic replied to the government of "Manchukuo" on January 12, saying that the tone used in the two documents of the "Manchukuo government" can only prove that the "Manchukuo government" is unwilling to peacefully resolve the border conflict caused by the Japanese-Manchurian troops and prevent similar incidents from occurring in the future, with the aim of clearly increasing the disputes between Mongolia and Manchuria. The Mongolian government pointed out in its document that "no one in the world can believe or will believe that the Mongolian people, who are devoting all their efforts to economic and cultural construction and deeply desire to maintain peaceful relations with neighboring countries, plan to fight with Japan or provoke Japanese-Manchurian troops." The Mongolian government pointed out that the "Manchukuo" Foreign Minister's accusations against the Mongolian government were unfounded and urged "Manchukuo" to pay attention to how the continued attack on the border guards of the Mongolian People's Republic and the refusal to take appropriate measures to resolve these disputes will endanger the peace policy. It also reiterated the requirement in the Mongolian government's document of December 22, especially to return the Mongolian soldiers captured from Mongolian territory. (16th TASS Dispatch)

Kulun Yesterday, at 9 a.m. on the 15th, the Mongolian border patrol team encountered Manchukuo troops invading the territory of the Mongolian Republic in a valley near Lake Hananur (25 kilometers from the border). The Manchu troops opened fire on the Mongolian soldiers. The Mongolian soldiers surrounded them. The Manchu troops wanted to escape, but they were all detained. There were a total of seven Manchu soldiers wearing military uniforms, seven Japanese rifles, a lot of ammunition, and seven horses were confiscated. There were no casualties on either side. At the same time, 30 yurts of the Bagut nomads were found in the same place. They were protected by the aforementioned Manchu troops to invade the Mongolian territory. They also said that the Japanese commanded the Bagut people's army in Manchukuo. This time they came under the orders of the Japanese. The Japanese told them that the Mongolian territory adjacent to Manchukuo was all Manchu territory. After the Mongolian side explained that the mines here were Mongolian territory and suggested that they return to Bargal, they all agreed and immediately turned back. (16th TASS Dispatch)

Registration of Real Estate Property Rights: No Need to Formulate Separate Regulations 56

Nanjing

The Executive Yuan has repeatedly received petitions from the people and various industrial and commercial groups stating that matters concerning the registration of real estate property rights should have legal restrictions for registration. The procedures for compulsory execution and auction, according to the provisional application of the rules for civil procedure execution, are still incomplete and a law should be formulated. The Executive Yuan requested the Legislative Yuan to review the matter. Sun Ke approved the request and referred it to the Civil Law Committee for review. The committee concluded that the Land Law already had provisions for the registration of real estate property rights, and there was no need to formulate separate regulations. Regarding the auction procedure, the Executive Yuan is drafting a law on compulsory execution, which will be included in it. Furthermore, the Executive Yuan's request to the Legislative Yuan to formulate a real estate mortgage law has also been reviewed by the Civil Law Committee and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan meeting for review on the 17th. (16th, Central News Agency dispatch)

Sun Lianzhong Leaves After Visiting Nanjing, Returns to Defense 57

Nanjing

Sun Lianzhong, Commander-in-Chief of the Sixteenth Route Army, finished his visit to Nanjing and boarded the Ningxing transport at 8:00 AM on the 16th to go to Hankou, then transferred to Xiang to return to defense. (16th, Special dispatch)

British Rescue Team Stationed in Afghan Border North Road Attacked by Three Italian Planes Again: 14 Dead, 35 Wounded; Geneva People Outraged Upon Hearing This 59

Taixi: The Geneva Red Cross rescue team led by British Major Pei Gang, stationed in Waldia Town between Taixi and Lake Agashi, was bombed by three Italian planes yesterday, killing 14 and wounding 35. Although Pei Gang's tent was destroyed, he was not injured. He immediately telegraphed for help. Soon, a British rescue team consisting of four doctors and twelve nurses rushed to Waldia overnight along rugged and dangerous roads. The remaining team members, under the guidance of Dr. Merrai, also rushed to help after dawn this morning. The Italian planes bombed for an hour. All medical supplies, food, and some local houses were destroyed by the flames from the incendiary bombs. The wind was strong at the time, and the fire spread faster. It is reported that the Italian planes dropped six 300-pound bombs. The 14 bodies that have been found are almost all women, elderly men, and children, and most of the injured are also elderly men and women. It is reported that the rescue team clearly displayed the Geneva Red Cross symbol when the Italian planes attacked. (16th, Reuters dispatch)

Geneva

The report of the Italian planes bombing the Geneva Red Cross rescue team in Waldia yesterday has aroused the indignation of the general public in Geneva. What exactly do the Italians want to do with such actions? This is the question that people are asking each other. The League of Nations Administrative Council will discuss Italy's destruction of the Red Cross's public affairs, and will instruct the Italian representative Arosio to explain everything. Some quarters believe that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini now wants to take the opportunity to withdraw from the League of Nations. (16th, Reuters dispatch)

Britain Still Intends to Participate in Oil Embargo Against Italy: League of Nations to Establish Special Committee 60

London

Reuters' diplomatic correspondent claimed that the rumour that the British cabinet had decided yesterday not to participate in the oil embargo against Italy had been denied by the authorities. Britain will definitely participate in any collective resolution on the oil embargo in Geneva. In addition to restating this principle, it is reported that the cabinet meeting yesterday did not give Foreign Secretary Eden any specific instructions, so Eden is free to turn the cabinet's intention into a real resolution in Geneva. The British government now firmly insists that the League of Nations' 18-nation committee appoint a special committee to study the facts and determine whether the oil embargo can be effective. Much of the work has already been completed by experts, so it is believed that this small committee can draft a report on the effectiveness of the oil embargo in a few days. (16th, Reuters dispatch)

London

After today's cabinet meeting, according to reliable sources, Foreign Secretary Eden has been ordered to recommend to the League of Nations' 18-nation committee that a small committee be appointed to discuss the oil embargo issue. Diplomatic circles here believe that the result of this recommendation will be an indefinite postponement of the kerosene embargo. (15th, National Telegraph dispatch)

Japan Formally Notifies Withdrawal from Naval Conference; United States to Add Battleships; Britain Plans to Issue National Defense Bonds; Japanese Army and Navy Plan Joint Defense 61

London

The Five-Power Naval Conference has completely failed today. Japan's demand for equality has been rejected. The Japanese delegation immediately withdrew formally and issued a declaration stating that it had no choice but to withdraw due to differences of opinion in the conference. (15th, National Telegraph dispatch)

London

The notification of Japan's withdrawal from the disarmament conference was personally handed over by Plenipotentiary Nagano to Chairman Monsell at 7:00 PM on the 15th. Chairman Monsell immediately understood and accepted it. Japan's break with the disarmament conference was decided on this evening. (15th, Electric Telegraph dispatch)

London

Japanese representative, Ambassador Nagai, declared to the press that the Japanese government will appoint two observers to stay in the naval conference. (15th, Havas Agency dispatch)

London

This agency's naval issue reporter has learned that after Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference, Britain sincerely hopes that the naval conference will continue among Britain, the United States, France, and Italy, and will no longer pay attention to Japan's obstructive measures. British people believe that Britain's territory is all over the world, so it cannot be compared with the Japanese navy, which can be concentrated in one place. Therefore, in terms of various countries, naval armaments equality and security equality have different meanings. (16th, Havas Agency dispatch)

London

The Daily Telegraph reported that during a meeting of the Cabinet Defense Committee yesterday, the ministers and military experts concerned studied the future operations of the army, navy, and air force, and realized that the army and air force are sufficient to undertake important tasks, but their strength is still unable to guarantee Britain's communication with its food sources. Therefore, it was decided to allocate funds to strengthen the army and air force. (16th, Havas dispatch)

London

The Cabinet Defense Committee held a meeting yesterday, attended by ministers from relevant departments. The importance of the defense measures to be taken is said to be above the expectations of the general public. According to the Manchester Guardian, "The part of the budget for national defense is nothing less than a major burden on the country. Germany's rearmament has long made Britain vigilant, but as Germany's military spending has been continuous in recent years, Britain's vigilance has increased day by day, which is undoubtedly true." (15th, Havas dispatch)

London The Cabinet Defense Committee met again at 10 Downing Street today, the third meeting this week. No experts were present, and Prime Minister Baldwin was still the chairman. It is heard that the joint meetings all focused on defense issues and defense financial issues. It is now believed that the government may issue national defense bonds. (16th, Reuters dispatch)

Washington

Japan's withdrawal from the London Naval Conference has prompted responsible parties to express that the US Navy Department will soon ask Congress for continued funding to build more battleships. It is heard that an experimental plan has been drawn up to modify two existing battleships or build a new battleship by the end of the year to fill the gap. This decision will proceed simultaneously with the procedure of building a navy according to the treaty. Senator Pittman, chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee, said that the plan to continue restricting naval armaments has now failed. Since Japan has withdrawn from the conference, the United States cannot agree with any other country to reduce its navy. Japan's withdrawal clearly means unlimited expansion of its fleet. (15th, Reuters dispatch)

Washington

Navy Secretary Swanson announced today that after the US fleet's spring exercise, four cruisers and twenty-four destroyers will cruise the Atlantic. Observers interpreted this announcement as meaning that most of the US Navy will be stationed on the West Coast. (15th, National Telegraph dispatch)

Tokyo

After receiving the telegram about the breakdown of the disarmament conference, the Navy immediately reported the course of the conference's breakdown within the Navy Department on the same day and notified the future policy. In order to thoroughly awaken the navy in the future, it was decided to convene the commanders of each fleet and the commanders of each major port at 10:00 AM on the 20th of this month in the department. The Naval Minister will report on the course of the meeting and give important instructions on the future policy. (16th, Allied dispatch)

Tokyo

The United Kingdom and the United States will have plans for Pacific defense and facilities in the future. The Army is now planning to establish a joint defense plan with the Navy, but the Japanese government's policy, although it has withdrawn from the disarmament conference, still intends to avoid the competition of expanding armaments as much as possible. Therefore, the Army also intends to maintain the status quo as much as possible for Pacific defense facilities and adopt a calm attitude. (16th, Allied dispatch)

The Last Meeting of the Five Powers 62

London

Japan has withdrawn from the naval conference. This decision by Japan was expected long ago. Yesterday afternoon, the first committee of the naval conference met for a long time. The Japanese representatives reiterated their demand for equality, and the representatives of other countries expressed their opposition. Therefore, the Japanese delegation decided to withdraw from the conference and issued a long article stating the reasons for its withdrawal and defending its proposal for a common maximum limit, saying that reducing or abolishing aggressive armaments is the most reasonable way to obtain a state of non-harm and non-aggression. In this way, the concept of security can be strengthened, and progressive disarmament can eventually be achieved. It also said that what we want to clearly state is that although we are withdrawing from the naval conference, we have no intention of engaging in an arms race. We are determined to always promote world peace and to promote world peace by carefully creating the best friendly relations with other countries.

British Naval Minister Monsell, who chaired yesterday, spoke freely about Britain's attitude towards Japan's proposal, saying that the Washington Treaty is the best guarantee of security. Britain, like Japan, wants to reduce its navy, but this reduction must be done in a way that is fair to all parties and does not harm the security of any country. From the British delegation's point of view, naval power cannot be measured by the number of ships alone, without taking into account other factors such as the distance of bases, the source of supply, and the vulnerability of transportation lines. A country with responsibilities all over the world must pay attention to its navy to protect its maritime communications. Therefore, its naval power must be higher than that of a country that can maintain its entire navy within or near its own territorial waters. Therefore, the British government and the public feel that Japan's proposal will create a situation unfavorable to the British Empire. Accepting this proposal is tantamount to suicide. Japan only has one sea that is closely related to its survival, while Britain must defend the roads of seven seas. If Japan's proposal is applied to all countries in the world, then all countries, no matter how weak their financial resources or how small their responsibilities, will not only have the right to build a navy equal to that of their neighbors, but will also be encouraged to increase their armaments. This plan is suitable for encouraging countries with existing small navies to greatly increase their armaments.

Britain's Five Points 63

In short, Britain's attitude can be divided into six points: Naval equality cannot be measured by the number of ships alone, but the distance of bases and the length of transportation routes must also be considered. Countries with larger navies cannot neglect the necessary defenses of their land and focus solely on fleets stationed in distant places. Countries with responsibilities all over the world must use their naval power to protect their entire transportation lines and the transportation between all parts, and must also have a greater naval power than countries whose entire fleet is in their own territorial waters. A common maximum limit is not suitable for the needs of the British Empire's defense, because the British Empire must consider its responsibilities in the European Sea, the Atlantic, and the Pacific. The Washington Treaty is the best guarantee of equality and security. Japan's proposal will cause Britain to encounter a bizarre situation, because this proposal not only allows all countries, no matter how weak their financial resources, to build ships to compete with their neighbors, but also indirectly encourages all countries to engage in shipbuilding competition. It feels that Japan's plan cannot be the basis for disarmament or restriction, and is deeply regretful, but it hopes that the Japanese delegation will continue to cooperate with other delegations to seek alternative methods to achieve the common goal of disarmament of all countries. (16th, Reuters dispatch)

London

In today's general committee of the naval conference, the arguments made by the representatives of the British Dominions all supported Britain's position. For example, the chief representative of Australia, Bruce, said that Japan's proposal has lost the original intention of restricting armaments and cannot achieve the goal of security equality. The chief representative of India, Birdlow, believed that there was no acceptable point in Japan's proposal. The arguments cited by the chief representative of Canada, Massey, were also very close to Britain's position. The chief representative of South Africa, De Wet, said that the common maximum amount proposed by Japan, if the limit set is appropriately increased, so that countries whose national defense needs are above those of other countries have room for maneuver for the sake of safety, then this proposal may be accepted. (15th, Havas dispatch)

Attitudes of France and Italy 64

London

French representative Vice Admiral Robert gave a speech at the General Committee of the Naval Conference this afternoon, saying, "Japan advocates that each naval country should have the autonomous right to decide on the naval force necessary for maintaining its security. France agrees with this proposition. Based on this principle, the security conditions of each country are different, and its naval armaments will naturally be different. However, what we do not understand is that if the naval armaments of each country should be equal to each other, just as the common maximum amount system proposed by Japan stipulates, even if the equal status is limited to so-called offensive warships, then how will this so-called equality make it compatible with the different national defense needs of each country? As a result, some countries will find it difficult to obtain sufficient security, while other countries will enjoy excessive protection, and then aggression and threats will arise, which all of us want to avoid, and the Japanese delegation also has the same mentality." Vice Admiral Robert then advocated that the naval conference should re-submit the compromise proposal put forward by France, that is, the suggestion of exchanging information on shipbuilding, and advocated the establishment of another committee to sort out France's suggestions, while the first committee should continue to cooperate with Japan, so as to continue to study other issues. This procedure of taking care of both sides should be sought immediately. (15th, Havas dispatch)

London

The General Committee of the Naval Conference met at 3:30 PM today. Italian Chief Representative, Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, spoke, saying that Italy fully agreed with the principles on which the common maximum amount proposal put forward by Japan was based. However, Italy was extremely opposed to strictly determining the total tonnage of the navy of each naval country by the current ratio system or by the common maximum amount system. In Italy's view, Japan advocates that the naval tonnage of each country should be differentiated according to its geographical location. How is this different in practice from the ratio system? Is the so-called strict egalitarianism not abandoned? (15th, Havas dispatch)

Hirota Issues Statement 65

Tokyo

Foreign Minister Hirota issued a statement today on the withdrawal from the naval disarmament conference. The full text is as follows: Maintaining international peace and contributing to its promotion is the consistent national policy of the Japanese government. When the London Naval Disarmament Conference was convened, Japan gladly participated, also based on this national policy. The Japanese government's policy of participating in this decision meeting is to ensure the firmness of national defense, reduce the burden on the people, and enhance friendly relations between countries through a fair and appropriate naval disarmament agreement between the countries concerned. The Japanese government then appointed Japanese representatives to propose at the meeting to set a common maximum limit that the naval forces of each country cannot exceed within the scope of not harming the sense of security of each country, and to reduce this limit as much as possible, so that each country can maintain armaments that are difficult to attack but have no defensive insecurity. It also advocated greatly reducing offensive weapons such as battleships, aircraft carriers, and class A cruisers, in order to realize thorough disarmament and establish the principle of non-threat and non-aggression. However, regardless of the efforts of the Japanese plenipotentiaries, Japan's fair and appropriate fundamental主張 was not accepted by the countries. Japan also hoped to solve problems with the possibility of resolution at the meeting, made a treaty, issued a joint declaration, stated that it would not engage in an arms race in the future, and sought to complete the meeting satisfactorily. However, Japan's sincerity was not recognized by the countries. Therefore, the Japanese representatives had no choice but to withdraw from the meeting. Although, whether or not the disarmament treaty exists, the Japanese government of course respects the spirit of non-threat and non-aggression. It goes without saying that there is no intention of inducing an arms race. The original intention of the Japanese government to cooperate in the disarmament cause for world peace has not changed. It sincerely hopes that the governments of all countries will understand the sincerity of the Japanese government's advocacy of armaments reduction as soon as possible. (16th, Allied dispatch)

American Newspaper Comments 66

Washington

International Editor Sins of the Shaw series newspapers commented on Japan's international policy in the Washington News today, saying that Japan's withdrawal from the London Naval Conference is closely related to Italy's suffering from the League of Nations' sanctions. Because Japan lacks natural resources, it is eager to control the raw materials of the Asian continent, and even wants to take the islands at the Pacific mouth to the south. In the end, it is difficult to avoid a war. Therefore, Japan's policy is to strive for the superiority of the army, navy, and air force. Japan does not want to be trapped in the League of Nations like Italy. If its navy can be equal to other countries, with the trust islands in the Pacific as bases for submarines and air forces, and mines are placed all over the Asian coastal islands, it will be difficult to predict victory even if Britain and the United States join forces to attack. As for the land, Japan is producing buffer states in Manchuria and North China, so that its land and air forces can move freely. In the future, in addition to Soviet Russia, it can also not fear any country. Since then, external development will be safer day by day. Japan is eager to have a sufficient supply of raw materials in both wartime and peacetime, so it is striving to gain more land in China. In the future, it may also plan to acquire air force bases in eastern Siberia, the Philippine Islands, and the Dutch East Indies. Then, the coal and iron of North China and Manchuria, the oil of Soviet Russia, the oil, coal, and rubber of the Dutch East Indies, and the various products of the Philippine Islands can all be obtained. If Japan can occupy the non-island, it can control a large part of the Pacific, so its naval strength is naturally indispensable. (15th, National Telegraph dispatch)

Germany Is Not Surprised 67

Berlin

German newspapers all said that Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference was inevitable. A local newspaper commented, "Japan is coming from Soviet Russia," and "The countries have no sincere determination to disarm, so the conference has been a failure from the beginning. The United Kingdom and the United States may establish a certain agreement, but the two countries cannot formulate any practical disarmament procedures without Japan's participation. At the same time, France and Italy will continue to compete." A certain newspaper headlined the news from London as "The United Kingdom and the United States Reject Japan's Naval Compromise." (16th, Reuters dispatch)

Berlin

Political figures did not express surprise at Japan's decision to withdraw from the naval conference, but believed that the Washington and London naval treaties had created a new situation between the signatory countries due to Japan's move. The Foreign Ministry stated that although Germany did not participate in the naval conference, it had been closely watching the development of the situation. Germany signed a naval agreement with the United Kingdom in June last year, and has already shown a spirit of compromise. At this time, it still hopes that Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference will not aggravate the current international tensions and cause shipbuilding competition. In addition, most newspapers commented on the naval conference, saying that the failure of the conference was actually unrelated to Germany. Among them, the Berlin Stock Exchange Daily reported that after Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference, the position of Britain and France themselves must be reflected upon, and used as an excuse to hope that Soviet Russia would send observers to participate in the conference, "so as to prevent the threat from the Soviet Union in the Baltic Sea." The Berlin local daily also spoke of the threat from Soviet Russia, and said, "Japan's withdrawal from the naval conference will be followed by Soviet Russia's joining. A farce in London is about to turn into a prank. I don't know that this kind of conference has long been coming to an end. Even if it is forced to continue, it will hardly be helpful for genuine disarmament." (16th, Havas dispatch)

Although it is unfortunate that Japan has withdrawn, the world still hopes that Japan will cooperate in this good and necessary work. Japan's attitude is clearly unreasonable, and there is no other way to explain it other than to say that those in power in Tokyo have no knowledge of the world situation outside of Japan, nor do they wish to understand it. No responsible Japanese politician would want to provoke the United States into a naval building competition. Southern Front: Intense Battle Between Italian and Abyssinian Forces; Italian Army Advances Fifteen Miles 70

Rome

The southern front is currently experiencing the most intense fighting since the start of the war. The Italian forces in that sector began their offensive on New Year's Day and were fiercely resisted by the troops under Abyssinian General Afewerki. However, they were eventually forced to retreat, and the Italian army pursued them. By January 12th, the Italian advance was blocked by the Abyssinian rearguard, leading to a fierce battle. Judging by the number of troops involved on both sides and the extent of the battle area, it can be considered a major engagement. The Italian army has so far advanced its battle line by fifteen miles. It is estimated that 500 Abyssinian soldiers have died, and 100 Italian soldiers have died. According to recent reports, the Italian front line now extends from Margabiyaga, on the border of British Kenya, through Shirbi, Moguro, Lama, and Biringdi to the Davi River. (Reuter, 16th)

Two-Hour Power Outage Plunges New York into Darkness; Subway Trains Stop Running, Leaving 60,000 Passengers Stranded 74

New York

One of the main generators at the local electric company suddenly exploded at 9:15 last night, immediately cutting off the power supply. As a result, many subway trains were unable to operate, stranding 60,000 passengers underground, unable to move forward or backward. Service was not restored until 11:15. Most hospitals, theaters, cinemas, and department store elevators were also affected. The city streets were dark, and cries could be heard everywhere. More than 500 manhole covers along the streets, which had been tightly sealed, were cracked open due to the explosion. The authorities immediately issued an alert and dispatched vehicles to enable police officers to patrol the city. Fortunately, residents of the city were not alarmed. (Havas, 15th)

Special Commercial News Telegram from Reuters, January 16th

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 140 shillings and 10 pence, up half a penny.

London Silver: The silver market was quiet today. Spot prices fell 0.1875 to 19 pence 875. India made purchases, while speculators sold.

Mount Li Silver: The silver market continued to decline at the opening today due to low London prices. The March futures price was 43.50-44.00, down 40 pounds.

Exchange Rates

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market today, the U.S. dollar remained sharply stronger. At 10:30 a.m., the British-American exchange rate was $4.965625, down 0.03125 from yesterday's U.S.-British closing price. It was quite firm in the morning. At 1:00 p.m., the price was $4.9575, down 0.01125 from yesterday's closing price.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton: The opening was stable. March futures rose 0.01 to 11.35, and May futures fell 0.006 to 10.97. Prices trended lower in the afternoon. The market lacked new interest, and merchants were generally waiting to see developments in Washington regarding the new agricultural control plan.

Liverpool Wheat: The wheat market opened this morning at better-than-expected prices. The one-week report on Russian wheat and reports from the Southern Hemisphere were favorable to the bulls. Although demand was not strong, prices were quite stable. At 1:00 p.m., March futures fell 0.0025 to 6 shillings and 8 pence.

Student Patriotic Demonstrations in Guangdong Province: Removal of the Signboard of the Guangdong Provincial Education Department; Authorities Organize Volunteer Corps to Accommodate Students 90

Guangzhou Communication: Since the first patriotic parade was held by students in Guangdong Province, there was an incident on the 30th of last month where two students from the National Guangdong College of Law, surnamed Liang and Mai, assaulted the military training director and coerced classmates to sign documents. The college immediately announced the expulsion of the two students and handed them over to the Garrison Headquarters for investigation. This matter had just subsided when students from Sun Yat-sen University launched a second demonstration parade on the 9th of this month. When they reached the Education Department on Huiai West Road, they went to the department to petition. Unexpectedly, the students removed the "Guangdong Provincial Education Department" signboard and carried it away. On the same day, some students from Guangya Middle School (formerly the Provincial First Middle School) also participated in the parade. After the parade, they returned to school and demanded that the school authorities grant a one-month vacation so that students could go to various villages to promote patriotism. The principal of the school, surnamed Huo, was not on campus at the time. On the 10th, the students held another meeting, and the atmosphere was tense. Military police arrived to persuade and explain, and order was restored. The authorities, seeing the growing momentum of the students in recent days, immediately discussed response measures to prevent any excesses. It was decided to organize enthusiastic patriotic students into volunteer corps and female students into nursing corps, allowing students to participate freely. Those who continue to attend classes as usual would not be forced. A Volunteer Corps Headquarters would be established at Sun Yat-sen University, with Chen Jitang appointing Garrison Commander Li Shuzong as the concurrent Chief Commander. The First Battalion Headquarters would be attached to the Sun Yat-sen University Headquarters, with Hua Zhenzhong serving as the concurrent First Battalion Commander and Rao Hanjie serving as the concurrent Second Battalion Commander. The Battalion Headquarters would be located at Guangya Middle School, with Ruan Baohong serving as the concurrent Third Battalion Commander. The Battalion Headquarters would be located at the Municipal Second Middle School. After the incident of the removal of the Education Department signboard, Zou Lu, President of Sun Yat-sen University, telegraphed all parties on the 10th, stating that he had failed in his educational duties and should be dismissed and severely punished to clarify responsibility and rectify the academic atmosphere. The Southwest Political Affairs Council issued three orders regarding this matter on the 10th, the original text of which is as follows:

"It is hereby ordered that national salvation and resistance to aggression are the Council's long-standing and greatest advocacy. For years, we have based all our efforts on this purpose, declaring to the people of the country and striving to promote progress without the slightest slackening. The facts are in evidence, and the whole country knows it. Recently, students, recognizing the increasing seriousness of the national crisis, have engaged in extracurricular promotion, parades, and demonstrations. Their patriotic enthusiasm is commendable. However, national salvation and resistance to aggression are major matters that cannot be accomplished with empty words or achieved by luck. Students, as the outstanding members of the country, should at this time intensify their practice of practical national salvation science as an urgent need to resist the enemy and defend against aggression. Even if they think of using speech and action to awaken the people of the country, they should make appropriate expressions within the scope of discipline. If they merely act on impulse and forget the fundamental plan, wasting time and neglecting their studies, they will not only harm the strength of resistance to aggression but also violate the original intention of national salvation. In order to implement the Council's long-standing advocacy and to fulfill the students' patriotic enthusiasm, it is imperative to concentrate the students' national salvation efforts and授以救國實用科學技能(provide them with practical national salvation scientific skills.)Therefore, the First Army Group Commander is specially ordered to organize a national salvation volunteer corps and a national salvation nursing corps, select a site, and properly allocate male and female students from various schools for enlistment and training to fulfill the students' aspirations for national salvation. The said commander should instruct all students to abide by this order, wait quietly for enrollment and training, and study national salvation academic subjects to deal with the national crisis and resist foreign aggression. This is our hope. This order."

"It is hereby ordered that student patriotic movements originate from loyalty, indignation, and enthusiasm. If there is no one to lead them, they will inevitably become undisciplined, and it is feared that malpractices will arise, resulting in a loss of national salvation power. Therefore, a national salvation volunteer corps and a national salvation nursing corps should be organized immediately, a site should be selected, and male and female students from various schools should be properly allocated for enlistment and training to fulfill the students' aspirations for national salvation and avoid being led astray. In addition to ordering the First Army Group Commander to comply and distribute orders, the Provincial Government is hereby ordered to inform them and instruct all schools under its jurisdiction to be informed of this order."

"This order is for compliance. In recent days, students from various schools have been holding national salvation movements. Now, during the winter defense season, local security is of utmost importance. It is sincerely feared that reactionary elements will take advantage of the opportunity to make trouble. Strict precautions should be taken to prevent any incidents. In addition to ordering the First Army Group Headquarters and the Guangdong Provincial Government, this order is hereby issued to the Provincial Government Headquarters, which should immediately comply and instruct the military and police under its jurisdiction to pay attention at all times and be well prepared, without the slightest negligence. Be sure. This order."

Chen Jitang issued a proclamation: "Now, I have received an order from the Southwest Political Affairs Council of the National Government, which states that the staff and students of various schools in this city are enthusiastic about national salvation and should be systematically organized. The Commander-in-Chief is instructed to send personnel to organize a national salvation volunteer corps and a national salvation nursing corps for strict training to fulfill their patriotic aspirations. Therefore, Garrison Commander Li Shuzong is immediately appointed as the concurrent Chief Commander to organize separately. All enthusiastic patriotic staff and students are expected to register immediately to participate so that the organization can be established and training can be intensified, in order to unite together and alleviate the country's distress. This proclamation. Commander-in-Chief Chen Jitang." (Evening of January 10th)

It lasted for two hours before they left with the loot. The bandits fired several shots to show their power when they were leaving. The total amount of loot was more than 500 yuan.

Lecture on History, Part 1: The Goal of Teaching National History in Primary and Secondary Schools 100

— Zheng Hesheng, Full-time Editor and Compiler, National Institute for Compilation and Translation

Foreigners often say that the Chinese are like a sheet of loose sand. The Chinese people’s concept of the nation has always been like a sheet of loose sand, lacking a sense of national unity. However, besides the nation, there are very solid family and clan groups. The Premier believed that the relationship between the Chinese people and the structure of the nation starts with the family, then extends to the clan, and then to the nation, expanding step by step in an orderly manner. The relationship between large and small structures is very precious. He advocated using the clan as a unit, reforming its internal organization, and then uniting it into the nation. But how can we accomplish this unification and achieve the goal of "transforming the family into the nation?" Naturally, we need a sense of patriotism. To cultivate this sense of patriotism, on the one hand, we must break the bad habit of "not concerning oneself with matters outside one's position" and follow Mr. Gu Tinglin's legacy of "every individual is responsible for the rise and fall of the world." On the other hand, we must promote the glorious achievements in history and cultivate a sense of self-confidence to arouse feelings of love for the country. Since Emperor Huangdi founded the nation, we have had a long history and a significant culture. Since the late Qing Dynasty, we have mistakenly believed the slander of foreigners, believing that our people originated in the West, inevitably making us the laughingstock of forgetting our ancestors. Even more, some people consider Emperor Huangdi and Emperor Yao and Shun to be non-existent figures, and Emperor Yu to be an animal on the Nine Tripod Cauldrons, which is tantamount to destroying the glorious history of our ancestors. Now, to stimulate patriotic sentiment, we should promote the great spirit and foundation of our ancestors. In recent years, the central government has worshiped the Huangdi Mausoleum and Zhou Mausoleum, which is the intent.

The patriotic movement should be the responsibility of those in government, and the people of the whole country should share the responsibility. Once the country is in danger, those with knowledge should offer advice, those with money should contribute money, and those with strength should contribute strength. Regarding this fact, there are countless examples in national history. For example, during the Spring and Autumn period, when the State of Qi attacked the State of Lu, the people of Lu prepared to fight back. A man named Cao Gui requested to see the Duke of Lu. His fellow villagers advised him that those in positions of authority would have their own plans and that he should not interfere. Cao Gui did not listen and insisted on seeing the Duke, offering his plans and advice for the battle, which indeed resulted in a great victory. Also, when the people of Qin were about to attack the State of Zheng, they had already reached the border of Zheng, but the government of Zheng was still unaware. A merchant from Zheng named Xian Gao encountered them on the road and falsely claimed to be acting on the orders of the Duke of Zheng, using his own twelve oxen to reward the Qin soldiers and sending someone to inform the government to prepare for defense. The Qin general Meng Ming knew that the plan had failed and withdrew his troops. Furthermore, during the Han Dynasty, there was an entrepreneur in Henan named Bu Shi, who originally became wealthy by herding sheep. At this time, Emperor Wu of Han was about to attack the Xiongnu. Bu Shi volunteered to donate half of his wealth to help the government in its efforts on the border. The government wanted him to become an official, but he refused, and when asked about his purpose in donating his wealth, he stated that the country was now going to fight the Xiongnu, and the virtuous should sacrifice their lives and those with wealth should contribute money so that the Xiongnu could be destroyed! When we look at the patriotic fervor of these ancestors, we can understand the source of victory for the states at that time. When we lecture on national history, we should make every effort to elaborate on these types of facts. Our country is now in a situation of internal and external troubles converging upon us. The divergence of opinions in national administration and the weakness of the people's patriotic thoughts are all reasons for the potential downfall of the nation. How should we remedy this? The cause and effect of rise, fall, governance, and chaos in history are clearly visible. Our country should conduct detailed research on this to cultivate the people's concept of patriotism. This is a small responsibility of our academic and educational circles to protect the country.

We should study the truth of society. The teaching of history should naturally focus on the rise and fall of the nation and the country, but at the same time, we must understand the truth of society to lay the foundation for transformation and advancement. Because the entire history, in addition to a few leaders, is entrusted to and contains the potential social forces of the majority of ordinary people. Therefore, discussing the traces of social evolution and the problems of today's society is not only the key point of research for sociologists, but also the focus of historians. In Chinese history, the center of records has always been great figures such as dynasties, emperors, generals, and so on, and no attention has been paid to the changes in the entire society and the rise and fall of the entire culture. In fact, not only is this the case in China, but Western historians in the past also advocated that the deeds of great men represent the entire history. For example, Carlyle's statement that "history is the biography of great men" can be regarded as the representative of this school of historical views. In his book "Heroes and Hero Worship," he elaborates on great men such as gods, emperors, religious figures, priests, writers, and poets, believing that their thrilling achievements left in the world are what formed the majority of history. It was not until the middle of the eighteenth century that a historian named Voltaire included the entire social life of an era in the scope of history. In his book "The Century of Louis XIV," the chapter on customs describes the moral, social, economic, artistic, and literary life of Europe from Shaliman to Louis XIII, which can be called the first work to produce a true history of civilization. Since then, there have been many Western historians who have paid attention to social history, which is innumerable.

Since the introduction of the new Western historiography into China, people have begun to pay attention to the study of social history. In 1922, the Chinese Educational Improvement Society held a meeting, and Mr. Liang Rengong proposed a "Transformation of Secondary School National History Textbooks" case. He believed that the current textbooks were all political in nature, but political history cannot include the entire history. Old-style political history focuses only on the rise and fall of dynasties and wars, and the changes in political trends cannot be explained. Although social and cultural matters are occasionally described after each dynasty, they are too brief and not coherent. Due to this shortcoming, students cannot get a clear impression of the work of their ancestors after receiving national history education, so they cannot develop a deep love for their motherland. Its faults are that the historical events taught are too far away from modern life, causing students to split their learning and life into two halves. Furthermore, the political phenomena that have changed little over the years are full of deceit and darkness, and students will only increase their conservatism or other bad habits when they read it, which is contrary to the education of democratic governance, and for these reasons, students not only cannot develop interest in the subject of national history, but also tend to dislike it. In order to correct inherent shortcomings and meet the new requirements of the times, Mr. Liang advocated replacing political history with cultural history. At the same time, Mr. He Bocheng also had a proposal: "The editing or lecturing of history should be based on explaining the evolution of social conditions in past dynasties so that students can understand how the current situation has evolved." The reason for his proposal is that the scope of history is very wide, and the materials are very complicated. If facts are researched only for the sake of facts, then it will be too difficult to start. Because the materials are complicated, it is not easy to choose them. In the primary and secondary schools, the teaching time of history is very limited. If only adults and major events are described, it is just like volcanoes and oceans are not enough to represent geography, and tigers and leopards are not enough to represent zoology. If a method of quoting out of context is used, then the history compiled or lectured will inevitably have no clear purpose due to different subjective views. In order to facilitate the selection of materials, there should be a certain standard when editing or lecturing history. The purpose of history is to enable students to understand how the current situation has evolved, otherwise the effect of history will not be obvious. In order to achieve this purpose, attention should be paid to the evolution of social conditions. This kind of proposal is the beginning of the creation of new historiography in our country, but this kind of historical work with social activities as the main body has not yet been published, which shows that this kind of attempt is not easy.

Regarding the study of social evolution, there are naturally many difficulties. Mr. He has already conducted detailed research on this issue. He said: "We have two particularly difficult areas in our research on the history of society: one is the material problem, and the other is the compilation problem. From the perspective of materials: first, the materials on social history are very lacking. For example, our Chinese Twenty-Four Histories can be regarded as a voluminous work, but there are very few materials on general society. Second, because of the lack of materials, we are often prone to making mistakes in our research on a social history, such as missing one or ignoring the whole. Third, fundamentally, most of the materials on social history are records of others, not obtained from our own observations. If we want to use them, we must first solve the various problems of their authenticity and errors. From the perspective of compilation: first, the scope of research is not easy to determine. It is very difficult for us to determine the extent to which a certain social phenomenon is popular in the entire society or only in a part of it. Second, the types of phenomena are not easily distinguished. A phenomenon often looks like politics on the surface, but in fact it is due to economic motives. There are also those that obviously belong to religion on the surface, but in fact their motives lie in politics. Therefore, it is not easy to distinguish which social phenomenon is a purely political phenomenon and which phenomenon is a purely economic phenomenon. Third, because it is difficult to distinguish the types of various phenomena, it is very difficult for us to study the causal relationship between them in various social movements. The causes of political movements are not necessarily in politics, and the causes of economic movements are not necessarily in the economy. There are many interactive and complex relationships that cannot be seen on the surface alone. Mr. He's remarks are indeed the truth that he has spoken after studying social history. We acknowledge that the study of social history is more difficult than any other part of history, and especially if we want to study Chinese social history, but we should find ways to break through these difficulties. As for the purpose of studying social history, it is naturally to understand the truth of social culture, because now the general public does not understand the situation of their own country's society too much, and they are very estranged from their own culture. If they want to reform society and promote culture, they have no basis, and since the import of Eastern and Western cultures, they have been imitating blindly, often losing their inherent features and falling into a state of chaos. In our study of the social history of our country, we should discuss the social organization, social customs, social economy, etc. in detail. As for our country's inherent culture, such as the system of philosophy and ethics, the trends of literary novels, and the inventions of science and architecture, etc., we must also make a comparative study, so that we can have a clear understanding of our country's social culture, and based on these studies, we can carry out transformation and promotion, and naturally achieve the spirit of promoting the nation or the country. I hope that we will make every effort to gradually complete it.

In summary, in teaching national history in primary and secondary schools, we should have a consistent proposition on society, the country, and the nation, that is, to focus on the training of citizens. As Mr. Fu Mengzhen said, use historical facts as role models to inspire patriotism, national upward mobility, discipline, national resilience, forward-looking enlightenment, public morality requirements, and nation-building role models. Using historical descriptions is more practical and moving than using empty words. The educational authorities have declared that the purpose of secondary school teaching is to cultivate healthy citizens and make them the backbone of the Chinese national organization, and its content is the full cultivation of scientific knowledge and the strict training of national morality, so that those who receive secondary school education have a complete foundation whether they study academic subjects or serve society. This course of history is a tool for training national morality, but here there is one point that should be noted, that is, the compilation or lecturing of teaching materials should focus on positive encouragement, not negative pessimism; should focus on effective encouragement, not superficial stimulation; should focus on the truth of facts, not blind propaganda; should focus on the research of truth, not false illusions; should focus on practical theory, not extravagant desires; and strive to make students have a righteous and bright attitude, a firm and unyielding spirit, and become healthy citizens. If we can inspire students' determination to love society, love the country, and love the nation through historical education, and thus extend it to people from all walks of life, catch up and save the country from disaster, then the teaching of national history in primary and secondary schools will have a successful hope, completed.

Local News

Passengers Carrying Silver Coins at the Station Should Exchange Them for Legal Tender at the Ticket Office. The Limit for Carrying Silver Coins Is 300. Those Exceeding the Limit Must Obtain a Passport; Otherwise, It Will Be Considered Smuggling. 101

The Ministry of Finance, based on a request from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, requested separate instructions to be issued to the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway stations and wharves regarding the exemption from seizure of silver coins and subsidiary silver coins that cannot be exchanged for legal tender. At the same time, a concise proclamation of the enacted methods for exchanging legal tender was issued to ensure widespread knowledge and avoid being treated unjustly. The Ministry of Finance replied yesterday, stating, "Received. Previously, reports indicated that local military police were not clear about the intentions of the regulations and often made things difficult for ignorant people carrying small amounts of coins. The Ministry telegraphed all provinces, cities, and military agencies on [Date] of December 1935, instructing local military police not to confiscate silver coins carried by people from areas where legal tender is not circulating, but to instruct recipients to send them to nearby exchange agencies for exchange into legal tender. Those ignorant people who are not aware of the government orders and carry silver coins should be immediately instructed to go to the nearest exchange agency and exchange them for legal tender. In order to exchange legal tender, there should not be any interception on the way, so as to cause disturbances. If there is any deliberate violation, people should be allowed to accuse and strictly investigate. Those who deliberately conceal and intend to smuggle or collect, transport, and profit for personal gain should be strictly punished according to the law once discovered. Passengers on ships who use silver coins to purchase tickets or carry silver coins outside of the prohibited price should be instructed to hand them over to the ship's accounting office to exchange for legal tender. This Ministry has also separately instructed the Ministry of Communications and the Chief Inspector of Customs to instruct them to comply. In addition, the number of silver coins that passengers are allowed to carry was approved in September 1934. Each passenger is allowed to carry silver coins. If they are not of inferior quality, whether single or double, merchants are allowed to transport them freely within 300 coins. If the above number is exceeded, a passport must be obtained; otherwise, it will be treated as smuggling and confiscated. All these are on file. If the stations encounter passengers carrying silver coins, they should notify the passengers in accordance with the above-mentioned methods and hand over all the silver coins for purchasing tickets, or more than three hundred silver coins and double coins outside the ticket price, to the ticket office of the station for exchange into legal tender. The station will then issue separate receipts for the silver coins used by passengers to purchase tickets, and for the silver coins exchanged for legal tender in addition to the ticket price, and send them to the nearby legal tender exchange agency for exchange into legal tender. If station staff take the opportunity to attempt to smuggle or collect, transport, and profit for personal gain, they should be severely punished according to the law once discovered. In addition to consulting the Ministry of Railways to instruct the various railway bureaus to comply, and to announce it at each station, please inform and circulate this notification."

Transportation of Legal Tender Should Be Facilitated to the Greatest Extent Possible. No Need to Check the Voucher for Transporting Public Goods. The Ministry Orders the Railway Bureau to Comply. 102

According to the Shenshi News Agency, regarding the transportation of silver legal tender on state-owned railways and ships, the Executive Yuan of the National Government previously decided that state-owned railways and ships should charge 50% of the fee for transporting public goods for the transportation of silver legal tender, except for those that are transported free of charge by the Central Bank, etc. The Ministry has ordered all railways to comply. Subsequently, the Traffic Departments of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus inquired whether it was necessary to check the voucher for transporting public goods, or whether they could simply charge 50% of the fee. The Ministry issued Order No. 591, stating that legal tender should be facilitated to the greatest extent possible. The reporting procedures should still be handled according to the usual practices of each railway, and there is no need for the Ministry to issue a voucher for convenience. However, the transportation of silver should still require verification of a passport or certificate before it can be accepted. After receiving the order, the two railway bureaus have instructed the Traffic Department to comply.

Silver Industry to Form a Committee to Study Lowering Interest Rates. The Decisive Issue Is Lowering Deposit Interest Rates. 103

After Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, Guo Shun, Rong Zongjing, Nie Lusheng, and others submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to lower interest rates and help the real economy, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Silver Industry Association were all instructed by the Ministry to handle the matter. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency learned from the Silver Industry Association yesterday that the Silver Industry Association has decided to hold a joint meeting after the general conclusion of each industry in 1935 to discuss specific measures. The decisive issue in lowering loan interest rates is lowering deposit interest rates. Because the loans of the silver industry all come from absorbing deposits. If the loan interest rate is only lowered, but the deposit interest rate is not lowered, it will not be possible to operate the business. Although the deposit interest rates of various banks and money houses are not the same, the highest interest rate of foreign banks is 5%, the highest annual interest rate of Chinese banks is 10%, and the highest monthly interest rate of money houses is 10%. As for the loan interest rates, the lowest interest rate of foreign banks, Chinese banks, and money houses is 6%, and the highest is 12-13%, which depends on the money market. In case it is implemented, there should be remedies for established deposits and loans. Therefore, it is heard that the Silver Industry Association will organize a specialized committee for specific research at the joint meeting.

1935 Financial Report of Two Railways. Net Profit Estimated at Over 1.75 Million Yuan. Year-End Bonus of One Month's Salary Given to Employees with Preference. 105

Regarding the issuance of the 1935 year-end bonus for the two railways, the Railway Bureau had previously listed a calculation table and submitted it to the Ministry for issuance. The Ministry of Railways issued Instruction No. 146, stating, "Received the submission and attached table. The net profit of the railway for 1935 is estimated at over 1.75 million yuan. According to regulations, 20% of the net profit is allocated as a bonus, which would only be enough to issue slightly more than half a month's salary. Municipal Government Proclamation: Assisting Cotton Merchants with Registration. 106

The Shanghai Sub-Office of the Central Cotton Adulteration and Mixing Prohibition Office previously handled the registration of cotton merchants in this city in accordance with regulations for statistical purposes.
